# Learning Full-Stack JavaScript Development: MongoDB, Node, and React

> Learn by doing! Learn full-stack JavaScript development by building a web application with MongoDB, Node.js, and React.js. Learn how to use Node as a web server and an API server, how to consume data and build user interfaces with React, and how to read and write data with a MongoDB database. React allows you to build full-featured, data-driven applications faster and more efficiently than what is

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237) | 3h 35m | Advanced | 81K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

## Table of Contents

### Chapter Overview

- **1. Introduction** (1 videos)
- **2. 1. Getting Started** (7 videos)
- **3. 2. React Fundamentals** (5 videos)
- **4. 3. Working with Data** (8 videos)
- **5. 4. Routing and History** (7 videos)
- **6. 5. Persisting Data** (7 videos)

> **[7:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=425)** Remember, the browser has to download the bundle, parse it, and then call the React and react-dom APIs to figure out what to render.
>
> **[7:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=432)** So while this is doing, we'll flash this "Loading" message for now.
>
> **[7:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=437)** So now we can run the commands.
>
> **[7:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=439)** We're going to need to npm run dev-server, to run the node server.
>
> **[7:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=446)** And we'll also need to npm run dev-bundler, to run Webpack.
>
> **[7:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=452)** When Webpack runs, it creates a bundle.
>
> **[7:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=456)** By default, the bundle's name is main.js, and it actually creates it under the dist folder, right here.
>
> **[7:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=465)** So to use that, we need to include it in our application somewhere.
>
> **[7:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=470)** For example, right here at the end of the body, we can do a script src tag, and the source, in this case, is just main.js.
>
> **[8:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=480)** And I think that should do it, let's test.
>
> **[8:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=482)** Refresh, and if you notice, it flashes a "Loading..."
>
> **[8:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/react-and-webpack?u=76281980&t=485)** message real quick, and then renders the React component.

### 3. 2. React Fundamentals

#### Why React?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] React is a JavaScript library that's entirely focused on one task, building user interfaces.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=6)** It follows the Unix philosophy of doing one thing and doing it well.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=10)** The React Library comes into packages, React and ReactDOM.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=14)** And when we talk about React, we generally mean both of these packages, but it helps to understand the difference between them and how they work together.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=22)** We use the React API to describe a user interface and the ReactDOM API to build that interface in the browser.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=30)** These two packages are designed to work together.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=33)** React is the what and ReactDOM is the how.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=36)** And we the developers deal mostly with the what.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=40)** Using the React language, we can tell ReactDOM what we want and ReactDOM takes our UI descriptions and figures out how to efficiently create them in a browser and how to update them as well when things get changed.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=55)** The update process is actually what's more impressive about React.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=58)** For that, React uses a programming concept known as the Virtual DOM to minimize Real DOM updates.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=65)** The big picture of this Virtual DOM concept is that every time React creates an HTML tree in a browser, it keeps a copy of that tree in memory.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=74)** Then when the app state changes and things need to change in the browser, React computes the new HTML version in memory first then it compares it with the current in browser HTML since that was kept in memory too.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=87)** And this allows React to figure out what exactly has changed before making any actual changes in the browser.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=94)** And then React only makes the changes that are needed, leaving everything else in the app as is.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=100)** You don't actually need to fully understand that in order to use React, but understanding it would certainly make you write better React code.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=108)** In this article, I go over this concept and many others in detail.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/why-react?u=76281980&t=112)** We're going to cover some of the other concepts in this article over the next few videos, but it would be great if you can give this article a quick read at this point in the course if you can.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Env Vars:** dom (3), html (3), api (2)
> **Code Keywords:** interface (2)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1), known as (1)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **Analogies:** picture (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### JSX syntax
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=1)** - [Presenter] So far we wrote a very simple React component, and configured the system to render it.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=8)** Npm run dev server, and this is here, is the current state of the application.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=14)** This syntax here, and also on line 10, right here, is called JSX.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=20)** Let's talk about what else can we do with JSX.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=23)** We can nest elements, just like HTML.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=26)** Let me put, Hello React, in an <h1>.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=29)** And in an <h2>, let's put another element.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=33)** Save and this is fine.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=34)** A component can return a tree of elements.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=37)** You can also inject dynamic JavaScript in here, using the curly braces syntax {}.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=42)** In here we can put any JavaScript call, and React will take the output of that call, and include it in the DOM.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=51)** These expressions in curly braces, are very handy for two popular cases.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=55)** When we need to conditionally render elements, and when we need to render elements, from a dynamic collection.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=61)** Let's talk about both of these cases.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=63)** First you need to understand, that if React sees a false expression, or a true expression or an undefined expression, all of these cases React will just ignore them.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=74)** It will do nothing with them.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=75)** It will not render anything.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=77)** This is great for conditional rendering.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=79)** Say that we want to, conditionally render this with JSX.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=83)** I can put it inside curly braces, and have a condition here, to output either the element, or false.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=91)** If the condition is false this whole expression will be false.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=95)** If the condition is true, this whole expression, is going to be the second element of the Boolean.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=101)** That's how the JavaScript && operator works.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=104)** It will return the second part of the expression, when the first part is true.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=108)** For an example of that, let's do Math.random() > 0.5, effectively making this a random binary call.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=115)** It's either true or false half of the time.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=118)** And if we do that, you'll notice that sometimes, with JSX will render, and other times it will not.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=126)** Very good.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=127)** The other thing about these curly braces, is to render a collection.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=131)** Say that we have an array of TODOS.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=135)** ["Learn React", "Build Something"] If I need to render this array in the UI, and do that in here, instead of using, let's say, a for loop, I'm going to assume, that this is a dynamic array.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=148)** Is it going to come somewhere from an API.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=150)** We don't control it, so we need to render it.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=153)** We can render it declaratively as well.

> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/jsx-syntax?u=76281980&t=190)** Basically the map call, transformed this array, into another array, that wrapped these texts in <li> elements. Exactly like this.

#### Component life-cycle and side effects
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Every React component has a life cycle.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=3)** First it gets rendered by React in memory then React mount the component into the DOM, then the component might be updated again in the DOM and it can also be removed from the DOM.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=17)** React provides method for us to execute code around these events in the life cycle of a component.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=23)** We can for example, do something after the component is rendered or right before it gets re-rendered or unmounted.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=31)** The simplest method to do that in React is with a useEffect function.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=37)** Just like useState, useEffect is a function to define a side effect for the component.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=43)** The use something functions in React are known as hooks.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=47)** They were introduced a few years ago as an alternative to the other method that we used before them, which is to use React class components.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=55)** And React still supports class components but using React hooks in function components is cleaner in my opinion, and I use it exclusively.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=64)** I covered the class method in the old version of this course if you're interested in learning it as well, which you might need to if you'll be working with an old code base for example.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=73)** React has a few other hook functions, but useState and useEffect are the ones that we tend to use the most.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=80)** Other hooks are for more advanced use cases and we'll talk about them if and when we need them.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=86)** So we call useEffect just like we called useState in a component and it takes as its first argument, a function.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=96)** React executes this function that we pass to it every time it renders the component.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=102)** So if we have a console log line here and if we test now, you'll see that line after the first render and every time the app component re-renders, which happens on button click, you're going to see this line again.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=118)** What can this be used for?
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=120)** Any integration with anything outside of React.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=123)** For example, to fetch data or call the DOM API, or collect information for analytics tools or start a timer, anything external to React, you can do in useEffect.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=135)** That's actually why it's named useEffect, it's used to introduce side effects to the component, calling a data API to fetch something as a side effect to rendering a component.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=145)** The return value of this function is significant.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=149)** We make it return another function and this return function is our chance to do any side effects cleanup when the component re-renders, or when it's removed from the application.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=162)** React will call this return to clean a function right before it re-renders the component.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=168)** To understand that, let's start an interval timer in here, setInterval call takes in a function and as a second argument, the interval in milliseconds so let's do one second.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=181)** So whatever code I'm going to write inside this function is going to be executed every second forever.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=188)** And how about we update the counter here as well so counter equal counter plus 1.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=194)** Let's take a look, refresh and the counter is going to be updated every second, just like that.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=203)** Now notice what happens if I click this button a few times.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=207)** You'll notice it's not really behaving as we design it, something else is going on here.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=212)** And this is happening because we are not cleaning up this side effect, this is a side effect, every time the component renders, a new interval timer is going to start, which means when I click the button, the component re-renders and another interval timer is going to start.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=229)** So with a few clicks, multiple interval timers are modifying this button right now.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=234)** So this cleanup function is our chance to do that cleanup.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=237)** For this example, we need to stop the timer and we can do that by getting the idea of the timer.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=243)** So this setInterval function returns an ID, let's put it in a constant, call it intervalID and to clean it up when React re-renders a component, we should clear the interval for that intervalId.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=259)** That's the syntax for setInterval and clearInterval.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=262)** So if we test now, the interval is running and if we click multiple times, you'll notice that button is behaving normally.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=271)** And that's because now when we click and re-render the component, we are stopping the current interval timer and starting a new one so there is no conflicting timers.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=282)** It's very important that we do this cleanup for any side effects that we introduce in a component.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=289)** It's not just about re-rendering the component, it's also about removing the component from the DOM.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=293)** If this component is getting removed from the DOM and we don't do the cleanup, you'll actually see errors because we're going to leave behind timers running, and those timers are going to try to update a component that does not exist anymore, and that's why we do the cleanup.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=308)** We actually don't need the cleanup for every useEffect, it's usually when we do asynchronous calls like this one that runs in the background.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=315)** In that case, we need to do the cleanup.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=318)** So for example, if your useEffect is to just console log a message, you don't need a cleanup for that and sometimes you need a useEffect to run under certain conditions.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=328)** For example, what if we want the useEffect to run only the first time the component is rendered and not every time it gets re-rendered.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=336)** Well, the second element of useEffect is an array and this array is a dependency array.
>
> **[5:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=343)** React uses the dependency array between component renders to determine if the effect should be called.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=350)** So if we leave an empty dependency array, it blocks the call for useEffect after the first one because the dependency array is the same, it did not change.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=358)** So now if we test this code, the first time the component renders, the useEffect is run and we see the console log.
>
> **[6:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=366)** If we update the counter, the useEffect is not called again because it has a dependency array that has not changed.
>
> **[6:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=373)** If we need to run the useEffect when the counter is updated, we just specify the counter value here so now when I click the button, the dependency will be different, it's one, it's two, now it's three and we see the messages.
>
> **[6:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=386)** This is a useful feature because it helps us control the logic of useEffect and only run it when it needs to be run.
>
> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=393)** And usually if you use a variable here, that variable should be part of the dependency array.
>
> **[6:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=399)** That actually is important to understand 'cause if you use a variable here and you don't specify it in the dependency array, then the value of that variable is going to be stale between re-renders.
>
> **[6:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=410)** Let me demonstrate that.
>
> **[6:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=411)** Let's go back to that interval example and instead of setCounter, let's just log the counter value here, just like that.
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=419)** So this is the normal behavior, the counter is not incremented but every second we log the counter value, so if we increment the counter, things work as expected.
>
> **[7:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=430)** Now, let's say that this useEffect has an empty dependency array, which means it will only run the first time.
>
> **[7:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=440)** What happens now is that when we refresh, the useEffect is run and it's console logging the counter value but when we increment the counter value, check it out, it's still rendering zero, why?
>
> **[7:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=454)** Because the value of counter here was not refreshed.
>
> **[7:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=458)** React only invoked this function the first time the component was re-rendered, thanks to the dependency array and after that, the function continues to render in memory with the same context that it was defined with.
>
> **[7:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=472)** So it's always going to see counter as zero because it was defined when counter was zero.
>
> **[7:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=478)** If we need to fix this problem then we have to specify counter as part of the dependency array so that when the value of counter changes, React recreates the function and use the new value for counter within that function.
>
> **[8:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=493)** And because we're using EsLint, the EsLint React hook plugin is going to warn us about that.
>
> **[8:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=499)** Right there it says you're using counter in a function and it's not part of the dependency array, and that's a problem.
>
> **[8:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=505)** if you need to specify multiple dependencies, it's just elements in the array.
>
> **[8:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=509)** You might actually be wondering why did we not specify the setInterval as a dependency?

> **[8:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=519)** If you use a function that you define in the component, that function should be part of dependencies but setInterval is a fixed function, it does not change and it's also outside the scope of this component.

> **[8:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/component-life-cycle-and-side-effects?u=76281980&t=531)** And the hook plugin actually tells us that this is an unnecessary dependency, you don't need need that.

> **[7:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/invoking-component-actions-in-children?u=76281980&t=442)** This however, is a bit of an advanced area in React.

> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=260)** The reason the state here is null is because we went back to a history record that was not pushed, it was the initial history record so it did not have any state associated with it.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=271)** If we actually go forward, you'll see that the popstate event has a state element which is the data that we passed to the history state API when we pushed this new history state, which is what we did here, we pushed this history data when we navigated to a contest, and the history API keeps that record for us to use later when we need to.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=294)** So let's handle the first case when there is no state.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=298)** So in here we can determine which page to render based on the state of the event, so let me create a new page constant, and we can rely on this statement, if there is a state and there is a contest ID on that state, then the new page is going to be contest, otherwise, the new page is going to be contest list.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=322)** This works for both cases when the state is null, or when the state does not have a contest ID.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=327)** We only need to navigate back to a contest if there is a contest ID in the record, which came from the contest ID data element that we added here when we pushed the state.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=337)** And the code that we need to deal with this new page is similar to this one, we need to set the page and set the current contest ID if we need to navigate to a contest.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=347)** The page that we need to set is the new page, and the contest ID is this value if it exists, right?
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=354)** So set current contest ID to be that value.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=359)** So that's it, read the state, see if there is a contest ID on the state, if there isn't, then we need to render the contest list.
>
> **[6:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=365)** If there is a contest id, we render the contest page, and we set the current contest ID to what's in that history state record.
>
> **[6:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=373)** This way we can navigate forward and backward in the state, and make the application aware of that navigation.
>
> **[6:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=379)** Let's test, refresh, go to the second contest, go back, and if we go forward, it goes back to that contest, because every time we go back or forward, there is a history state record for the previous page, and if it is a contest page it will have the contest id.
>
> **[6:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=396)** That's why we did if there is a contest ID, set it, and set the page to contest.
>
> **[6:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-full-stack-javascript-development-mongodb-node-and-react-15581237/handling-browser-navigation-history?u=76281980&t=401)** Now this is a really simple example for working with the history API, and there are a lot more complexities around this simple usage, but the core of the idea is that you push a record to a state when you need to navigate to a new page, associate some data with it, that data is what represents the state that you're pushing, and then you add a handler to deal with the back and forward clicks in the browser, and every time there's an event, you can read the previous history state that you pushed and use it for your application logic.
